<p><b>Düsseldorf</b> (<small>German:</small> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ˈdʏsl̩dɔɐ̯f]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:De-D%C3%BCsseldorf.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a4/De-D%C3%BCsseldorf.ogg" class="internal" title="De-Düsseldorf.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>, <a href="/wiki/Low_Franconian" class="mw-redirect" title="Low Franconian">Low Franconian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ripuarian_language" title="Ripuarian language">Ripuarian</a>: <i>Düsseldörp</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ˈdʏsl̩dœɐ̯p]</span>) is the capital city of the <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> state of <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Germany_with_more_than_100,000_inhabitants" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in Germany with more than 100,000 inhabitants">seventh most populous city in Germany.</a><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Düsseldorf is an international business and financial centre, renowned for its fashion and trade fairs.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The city is headquarters to one <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Fortune Global 500</a> and two <a href="/wiki/DAX" title="DAX">DAX</a> companies. <a href="/wiki/Messe_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Messe Düsseldorf">Messe Düsseldorf</a> organises nearly one fifth of premier trade shows.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Düsseldorf is known for its <a href="/wiki/Kunstakademie_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Kunstakademie Düsseldorf">academy of fine arts</a> (<a href="/wiki/Joseph_Beuys" title="Joseph Beuys">Joseph Beuys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_Leutze" title="Emanuel Leutze">Emanuel Leutze</a>, <a href="/wiki/August_Macke" title="August Macke">August Macke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Richter" title="Gerhard Richter">Gerhard Richter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigmar_Polke" title="Sigmar Polke">Sigmar Polke</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Andreas_Gursky" title="Andreas Gursky">Andreas Gursky</a>), its pioneering influence on electronic/experimental music (<a href="/wiki/Kraftwerk" title="Kraftwerk">Kraftwerk</a>) and its <a href="/wiki/Japanese_community_of_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Japanese community of Düsseldorf">Japanese community</a>. On the river <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a>, Düsseldorf holds <a href="/wiki/Rhenish_Carnival" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhenish Carnival">Rhenish Carnival</a> celebrations every year in February / March.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> It is one of the central cities of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr" title="Rhine-Ruhr">Rhine-Ruhr</a> metropolitan area. <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Most_Livable_Cities" class="mw-redirect" title="World's Most Livable Cities">Mercer's 2012 Quality of Living survey</a> ranked Düsseldorf the sixth most livable city in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Mercer_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mercer-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forbes_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(December 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Timeline of Düsseldorf">Timeline of Düsseldorf</a></div>
<p>When the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> was strengthening its position throughout Europe, a few <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic tribes</a> clung on in <a href="/wiki/Marsh" title="Marsh">marshy</a> territory off the eastern banks of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 7th and 8th centuries, the odd <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">farming</a> or <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a> settlement could be found at the point where the small river <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCssel" title="Düssel">Düssel</a> flows into the Rhine. It was from such settlements that the city of Düsseldorf grew.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Duesseldorf-Kupferstich-Merian.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Duesseldorf-Kupferstich-Merian.png/220px-Duesseldorf-Kupferstich-Merian.png" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Duesseldorf-Kupferstich-Merian.png/330px-Duesseldorf-Kupferstich-Merian.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Duesseldorf-Kupferstich-Merian.png/440px-Duesseldorf-Kupferstich-Merian.png 2x" data-file-width="2556" data-file-height="1620" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Duesseldorf-Kupferstich-Merian.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Düsseldorf in 1647</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first written mention of Düsseldorf (then called <i>Dusseldorp</i> in the local <a href="/wiki/Meuse-Rhenish" title="Meuse-Rhenish">Low Rhenish</a> dialect) dates back to 1135. Under <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick I, Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor Friedrich Barbarossa</a> the small town of <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf-Kaiserswerth" title="Düsseldorf-Kaiserswerth">Kaiserswerth</a> to the north of Düsseldorf became a well-fortified outpost, where soldiers kept a watchful eye on every movement on the Rhine. Kaiserswerth eventually became a suburb of Düsseldorf in 1929.</p>
<p>In 1186, Düsseldorf came under the rule of the Counts of <a href="/wiki/County_of_Berg" class="mw-redirect" title="County of Berg">Berg</a>. 14 August 1288 is one of the most important dates in the history of Düsseldorf. On this day the sovereign Count <a href="/wiki/Adolf_VIII_of_Berg" title="Adolf VIII of Berg">Adolf VIII of Berg</a> granted the village on the banks of the Düssel <a href="/wiki/Town_privileges" title="Town privileges">town privileges</a>. Before this, a bloody struggle for power had taken place between the Archbishop of <a href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Cologne" class="mw-redirect" title="Archbishopric of Cologne">Cologne</a> and the count of <a href="/wiki/County_of_Berg" class="mw-redirect" title="County of Berg">Berg</a>, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Worringen" title="Battle of Worringen">Battle of Worringen</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The Archbishop of Cologne's forces were wiped out by the forces of the count of <a href="/wiki/County_of_Berg" class="mw-redirect" title="County of Berg">Berg</a> who were supported by citizens and farmers of Cologne and Düsseldorf, paving the way for Düsseldorf's elevation to city status, which is commemorated today by a monument on the Burgplatz. The custom of turning cartwheels is credited to the children of Düsseldorf. There are variations of the origin<sup id="cite_ref-de.wikipedia.org_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de.wikipedia.org-11">[11]</a></sup> of the cartwheeling children. Today the symbol (Der Radschläger)<sup id="cite_ref-de.wikipedia.org_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de.wikipedia.org-11">[11]</a></sup> represents the story and every year the Düsseldorfers celebrate by having a cartwheeling contest. After this battle the relationship between the four cities deteriorated, because they were commercial rivals; it is often said that there is a kind of hostility between the citizens of Cologne and Düsseldorf. Today, it finds its expression mainly in a humorous form (especially during the Rhineland <i><a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">Karneval</a></i>) and in sports.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jan_van_der_Heyden_and_Adriaen_van_de_Velde_-_View_of_D%C3%BCsseldorf_with_the_church_of_St._Andrew_in_the_centre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Jan_van_der_Heyden_and_Adriaen_van_de_Velde_-_View_of_D%C3%BCsseldorf_with_the_church_of_St._Andrew_in_the_centre.jpg/225px-Jan_van_der_Heyden_and_Adriaen_van_de_Velde_-_View_of_D%C3%BCsseldorf_with_the_church_of_St._Andrew_in_the_centre.jpg" width="225" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Jan_van_der_Heyden_and_Adriaen_van_de_Velde_-_View_of_D%C3%BCsseldorf_with_the_church_of_St._Andrew_in_the_centre.jpg/338px-Jan_van_der_Heyden_and_Adriaen_van_de_Velde_-_View_of_D%C3%BCsseldorf_with_the_church_of_St._Andrew_in_the_centre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Jan_van_der_Heyden_and_Adriaen_van_de_Velde_-_View_of_D%C3%BCsseldorf_with_the_church_of_St._Andrew_in_the_centre.jpg/450px-Jan_van_der_Heyden_and_Adriaen_van_de_Velde_-_View_of_D%C3%BCsseldorf_with_the_church_of_St._Andrew_in_the_centre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jan_van_der_Heyden_and_Adriaen_van_de_Velde_-_View_of_D%C3%BCsseldorf_with_the_church_of_St._Andrew_in_the_centre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of Düsseldorf with the church of <a href="/wiki/St._Andreas,_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="St. Andreas, Düsseldorf">St. Andrew</a> in the centre, 1667, by <a href="/wiki/Adriaen_van_de_Velde" title="Adriaen van de Velde">Adriaen van de Velde</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Market_square" title="Market square">market square</a> sprang up on the banks of the Rhine and the square was protected by <a href="/wiki/Defensive_wall" title="Defensive wall">city walls</a> on all four sides. In 1380, the dukes of <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Berg" title="Duchy of Berg">Berg</a> moved their seat to the town and Düsseldorf was made regional capital of the Duchy of Berg. During the following centuries several famous landmarks were built, including the <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_church" title="Collegiate church">Collegiate Church of St Lambertus</a>. In 1609, the ducal line of the <a href="/wiki/United_Duchies_of_J%C3%BClich-Cleves-Berg" title="United Duchies of Jülich-Cleves-Berg">United Duchies of Jülich-Cleves-Berg</a> died out, and after a virulent struggle over succession, Jülich and Berg fell to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Wittelsbach" title="House of Wittelsbach">Wittelsbach</a> Counts of <a href="/wiki/Palatinate-Neuburg" title="Palatinate-Neuburg">Palatinate-Neuburg</a>, who made Düsseldorf their main domicile, even after they inherited the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_the_Palatinate" class="mw-redirect" title="Electorate of the Palatinate">Electorate of the Palatinate</a>, in 1685, becoming now <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">Prince-electors</a> as Electors Palatine.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadt_D%C3%BCsseldorf_1899.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Stadt_D%C3%BCsseldorf_1899.jpg/220px-Stadt_D%C3%BCsseldorf_1899.jpg" width="220" height="312" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Stadt_D%C3%BCsseldorf_1899.jpg/330px-Stadt_D%C3%BCsseldorf_1899.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Stadt_D%C3%BCsseldorf_1899.jpg/440px-Stadt_D%C3%BCsseldorf_1899.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2387" data-file-height="3384" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadt_D%C3%BCsseldorf_1899.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bond of the town Düsseldorf, issued 26. July 1899</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NRW,_Dusseldorf,_Rheinturm_-_view_to_Landtag.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/NRW%2C_Dusseldorf%2C_Rheinturm_-_view_to_Landtag.jpg/220px-NRW%2C_Dusseldorf%2C_Rheinturm_-_view_to_Landtag.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/NRW%2C_Dusseldorf%2C_Rheinturm_-_view_to_Landtag.jpg/330px-NRW%2C_Dusseldorf%2C_Rheinturm_-_view_to_Landtag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/NRW%2C_Dusseldorf%2C_Rheinturm_-_view_to_Landtag.jpg/440px-NRW%2C_Dusseldorf%2C_Rheinturm_-_view_to_Landtag.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NRW,_Dusseldorf,_Rheinturm_-_view_to_Landtag.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Landtag_of_North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="Landtag of North Rhine-Westphalia">state parliament</a>, seen from the top of the <a href="/wiki/Rheinturm" title="Rheinturm">Rheinturm</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rheinturm_D%C3%BCsseldorf_NRW_mit_Sternschnuppe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Rheinturm_D%C3%BCsseldorf_NRW_mit_Sternschnuppe.jpg/220px-Rheinturm_D%C3%BCsseldorf_NRW_mit_Sternschnuppe.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Rheinturm_D%C3%BCsseldorf_NRW_mit_Sternschnuppe.jpg/330px-Rheinturm_D%C3%BCsseldorf_NRW_mit_Sternschnuppe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Rheinturm_D%C3%BCsseldorf_NRW_mit_Sternschnuppe.jpg/440px-Rheinturm_D%C3%BCsseldorf_NRW_mit_Sternschnuppe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1620" data-file-height="1080" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rheinturm_D%C3%BCsseldorf_NRW_mit_Sternschnuppe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rheinturm Düsseldorf 70th Anniversary of the state NRW Illumination with <a href="/wiki/Rheinkomet" title="Rheinkomet">Rheinkomet</a>, including a real comet at the right side</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Under the art loving <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wilhelm,_Elector_Palatine" title="Johann Wilhelm, Elector Palatine">Johann Wilhelm II</a> (r. 1690–1716), a vast <a href="/wiki/Art_museum" title="Art museum">art gallery</a> with a huge selection of paintings and sculptures, were housed in the <i>Stadtschloss</i> (city castle). After his death, the city fell on hard times again, especially after Elector <a href="/wiki/Charles_Theodore,_Elector_of_Bavaria" title="Charles Theodore, Elector of Bavaria">Charles Theodore</a> inherited Bavaria and moved the electoral court to <a href="/wiki/Munich,_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Munich, Germany">Munich</a>. With him he took the <a href="/wiki/Collection_(museum)" class="mw-redirect" title="Collection (museum)">art collection</a>, which became part of what is now the <a href="/wiki/Alte_Pinakothek" title="Alte Pinakothek">Alte Pinakothek</a> in Munich. Destruction and poverty struck Düsseldorf after the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>. <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> made Berg a <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Berg" title="Grand Duchy of Berg">Grand Duchy</a> and Düsseldorf its capital. <a href="/wiki/Johann_Christian_Claudius_Devaranne" title="Johann Christian Claudius Devaranne">Johann Devaranne</a>, a leader of <a href="/wiki/Solingen" title="Solingen">Solingen</a>'s resistance to Napoleon's conscription decrees, was executed here in 1813. After Napoleon's defeat, the whole <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">Rhineland</a> including Berg was given to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Kingdom of Prussia</a> in 1815. The <a href="/wiki/Rhine_Province" title="Rhine Province">Rhine Province</a>'s parliament was established in Düsseldorf.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (December 2014)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> By the mid-19th century, Düsseldorf enjoyed a revival thanks to the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> as the city boasted 100,000 inhabitants by 1882; the figure doubled in 1892. In 1920, Düsseldorf became the centre of the General Strike. On 15 April 1920, 45 delegates of the German Miners Union were murdered by the <a href="/wiki/Freikorps" title="Freikorps">Freikorps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city was a target of <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II" title="Strategic bombing during World War II">strategic bombing during World War II</a>, particularly during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Ruhr" title="Battle of the Ruhr">RAF bombing campaign in 1943</a> when over 700 bombers were used in a single night. Raids continued late into the war. As part of <a href="/wiki/Oil_Campaign_of_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil Campaign of World War II">the campaign against German oil facilities</a>, the RAF raid of 20–21 February on the Rhenania Ossag refinery in the Reisholz district of the city halted oil production there. The Allied ground advance into Germany reached Düsseldorf in mid-April 1945. The <a href="/wiki/97th_Infantry_Division_(United_States)" title="97th Infantry Division (United States)">United States 97th Infantry Division</a> easily captured the city on 18 April 1945,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> after the local <a href="/wiki/German_Resistance" class="mw-redirect" title="German Resistance">German Resistance</a> group launched <a href="/wiki/Aktion_Rheinland" title="Aktion Rheinland">Aktion Rheinland</a>.</p>
<p>In 1946, Düsseldorf was made capital of the new <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federal state</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a>. The city's reconstruction proceeded at a frantic pace and the economic transformation guided Düsseldorf's economic growth.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_geography">Physical geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Physical geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/220px-D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/330px-D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/440px-D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Düsseldorf skyline</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rheinuferpromenade_in_D%C3%BCsseldorf_DSCF1161.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Rheinuferpromenade_in_D%C3%BCsseldorf_DSCF1161.jpg/220px-Rheinuferpromenade_in_D%C3%BCsseldorf_DSCF1161.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Rheinuferpromenade_in_D%C3%BCsseldorf_DSCF1161.jpg/330px-Rheinuferpromenade_in_D%C3%BCsseldorf_DSCF1161.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Rheinuferpromenade_in_D%C3%BCsseldorf_DSCF1161.jpg/440px-Rheinuferpromenade_in_D%C3%BCsseldorf_DSCF1161.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3840" data-file-height="2880" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rheinuferpromenade_in_D%C3%BCsseldorf_DSCF1161.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Promenade along the Rhine</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Düsseldorf lies at the centre of the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Rhine" title="Lower Rhine">Lower Rhine</a> basin, where the delta of the <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCssel" title="Düssel">Düssel</a> flows into the Rhine. The city lies on the east side of the Rhine, except <a href="/wiki/District_4,_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="District 4, Düsseldorf">District 4</a> (<a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf-Oberkassel" title="Düsseldorf-Oberkassel">Oberkassel</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf-Niederkassel" title="Düsseldorf-Niederkassel">Niederkassel</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf-Heerdt" title="Düsseldorf-Heerdt">Heerdt</a> and <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf-L%C3%B6rick" title="Düsseldorf-Lörick">Lörick</a>). Across the Rhine, the city of <a href="/wiki/Neuss" title="Neuss">Neuss</a> stands on the delta of the <a href="/wiki/Erft" title="Erft">Erft</a>. Düsseldorf lies southwest of the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> urban area, and in the middle of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr" title="Rhine-Ruhr">Rhine-Ruhr</a> metropolitan region.</p>
<p>Düsseldorf is built entirely on <a href="/wiki/Alluvium" title="Alluvium">alluvium</a>, mud, sand, clay and occasionally gravel. The highest point in Düsseldorf is the top of Sandberg in the far eastern part of the city (<a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf-Hubbelrath" title="Düsseldorf-Hubbelrath">Hubbelrath</a> borough) at 165 metres (541&#160;ft). The lowest point is at the far northern end in <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf-Wittlaer" class="mw-redirect" title="Düsseldorf-Wittlaer">Wittlaer</a> borough where the Schwarzbach enters the Rhine, with an average elevation of 28 metres (92&#160;ft).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjacent_cities_and_districts">Adjacent cities and districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Adjacent cities and districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following districts and cities border Düsseldorf (clockwise starting from the north): the <a href="/wiki/Duisburg" title="Duisburg">City of Duisburg</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mettmann_(district)" title="Mettmann (district)">District of Mettmann</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ratingen" title="Ratingen">Ratingen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mettmann" title="Mettmann">Mettmann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erkrath" title="Erkrath">Erkrath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hilden" title="Hilden">Hilden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Langenfeld,_Rhineland" title="Langenfeld, Rhineland">Langenfeld</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Monheim_am_Rhein" title="Monheim am Rhein">Monheim</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Rhein-Kreis_Neuss" title="Rhein-Kreis Neuss">District of Neuss</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dormagen" title="Dormagen">Dormagen</a>, Neuss, and <a href="/wiki/Meerbusch" title="Meerbusch">Meerbusch</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Like the rest of the lower <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">Rhineland</a>, Düsseldorf experiences moderate winters with little snowfall and mild to warm summers. The average annual temperature is 10.6&#160;°C (51&#160;°F) with an average yearly precipitation of 797 millimetres (31&#160;in). The dominant wind direction is from the west with velocities in the range of 3 to 4&#160;m/s (7–9&#160;mph), with gusts of 3.5 −4.8&#160;m/s (8–10.7&#160;mph). The wind is calm (defined as being under 2&#160;m/s or 4.5&#160;mph) about 35% of the time, more frequently at night and in the winter.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>

<p>With a population of 612,178 within the city boundaries (31 December 2015),<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Düsseldorf is <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Germany_by_population" title="List of cities in Germany by population">Germany's seventh largest city</a>. Its population surpassed the threshold of 100,000 inhabitants during the height of industrialisation in 1882, and peaked at just over 705,000 in 1962. The city then began to lose residents with many moving into neighbouring municipalities. However, since the late 1990s, the city's population has been slowly rising again.</p>
<p>A total of 109,883<sup id="cite_ref-Statistisches_Jahrbuch_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statistisches_Jahrbuch-16">[16]</a></sup> of Düsseldorf's population are foreigners (31 December 2008), the majority of whom come from within <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> (81,742). The largest <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">national minorities</a> are <a href="/wiki/Turks_in_Germany" title="Turks in Germany">Turks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks_in_Germany" title="Greeks in Germany">Greeks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Poles_in_Germany" title="Poles in Germany">Poles</a>. Düsseldorf and its surroundings have the third-largest <a href="/wiki/Japanese_community_of_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Japanese community of Düsseldorf">Japanese community</a> in Europe and the largest in Germany (about 11,000 people).<sup id="cite_ref-virtualtourist.com_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-virtualtourist.com-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Japantag_in_D.C3.BCsseldorf:_Welcome_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Japantag_in_D.C3.BCsseldorf:_Welcome-19">[19]</a></sup> Düsseldorf has the third-largest <a href="/wiki/Jews_in_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Jews in Germany">Jewish community</a> in Germany, with about 7,600 members.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mayors">Mayors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Mayors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="List of mayors of Düsseldorf">List of mayors of Düsseldorf</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Districts">Districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Districts of Düsseldorf">Districts of Düsseldorf</a></div>
<p>Since 1975, Düsseldorf is divided into ten administrative districts. Each district (<i>Bezirk</i>) has its own elected district council (Bezirksvertretung) and its own district mayor (Bezirksvorsteher). The district councils are advisory only. Each district is further subdivided into boroughs. There are 50 boroughs in Düsseldorf.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
