<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:D_medienhafen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/D_medienhafen.jpg/220px-D_medienhafen.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/D_medienhafen.jpg/330px-D_medienhafen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/D_medienhafen.jpg/440px-D_medienhafen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="665" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:D_medienhafen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Rheinturm" title="Rheinturm">Rheinturm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Gehry" title="Frank Gehry">Gehry</a>-buildings <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Neue_Zollhof" class="mw-redirect" title="Der Neue Zollhof">Der Neue Zollhof</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf-Hafen" title="Düsseldorf-Hafen">Hafen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%BCsseldorf_K%C3%B6nigsallee.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/D%C3%BCsseldorf_K%C3%B6nigsallee.jpg/220px-D%C3%BCsseldorf_K%C3%B6nigsallee.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/D%C3%BCsseldorf_K%C3%B6nigsallee.jpg/330px-D%C3%BCsseldorf_K%C3%B6nigsallee.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/D%C3%BCsseldorf_K%C3%B6nigsallee.jpg/440px-D%C3%BCsseldorf_K%C3%B6nigsallee.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%BCsseldorf_K%C3%B6nigsallee.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsallee" title="Königsallee">Königsallee</a> in <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf-Stadtmitte" title="Düsseldorf-Stadtmitte">Stadtmitte</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Düsseldorf has become one of the top <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" class="mw-redirect" title="Telecommunications">telecommunications</a> centres in Germany. With two of the four big German providers of mobile frequencies, <a href="/wiki/Vodafone" title="Vodafone">D2 Vodafone</a> and <a href="/wiki/E-Plus" title="E-Plus">E-Plus</a>, Düsseldorf leads the German <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile phone</a> market. There are many foreign information and communication technology companies in Düsseldorf such as <a href="/wiki/Huawei" title="Huawei">Huawei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Telegraph_and_Telephone" title="Nippon Telegraph and Telephone">NTT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ericsson" title="Ericsson">Ericsson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">Nokia</a>, and GTS.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. There are 18 <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">internet service providers</a> located in the capital of North-Rhine Westphalia. There are two airlines with headquarters in the city: <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a> and formerly independent <a href="/wiki/LTU_International" title="LTU International">LTU International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many of the internet companies in Düsseldorf have their roots in the world of advertising: there are 400 <a href="/wiki/Advertising_agency" title="Advertising agency">advertising agencies</a> in Düsseldorf, among them three of the largest in Germany: <a href="/wiki/BBDO" title="BBDO">BBDO Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Publicis" title="Publicis">Publicis</a>. A number of affiliates of foreign agencies deserve mention as well, such as <a href="/wiki/Ogilvy_%26_Mather" title="Ogilvy &amp; Mather">Ogilvy &amp; Mather</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dentsu" title="Dentsu">Dentsu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hakuhodo" title="Hakuhodo">Hakuhodo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/DDB_Worldwide" title="DDB Worldwide">DDB</a>. There are also about 200 <a href="/wiki/Publishing" title="Publishing">publishing houses</a> in Düsseldorf. There are around 170 national and <a href="/wiki/Global_financial_system" title="Global financial system">international financial institutions</a>, and about 130 insurance agencies, and one of Germany's eight <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchanges</a>. Several other major companies have their headquarters in the city: <a href="/wiki/Peek_%26_Cloppenburg" title="Peek &amp; Cloppenburg">Peek &amp; Cloppenburg</a> (fashion), <a href="/wiki/L%27Or%C3%A9al" title="L'Oréal">L'Oréal</a> Germany (Cosmetics and Beauty); <a href="/wiki/Henkel" title="Henkel">Henkel</a> AG &amp; Co. KGaA (Branded Consumer Goods and Industrial technologies); <a href="/wiki/Metro_AG" title="Metro AG">Metro</a> (wholesale, retail); Ergo (insurance), <a href="/wiki/Esprit_Holdings" title="Esprit Holdings">Esprit Holdings</a> (fashion, headquarters in Ratingen near Düsseldorf), BASF Personal Care &amp; Nutrition (formerly <a href="/wiki/Cognis" title="Cognis">Cognis</a> - chemicals, headquarter in Monheim near Düsseldorf, but production mainly in Düsseldorf).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Daimler_AG" title="Daimler AG">Daimler AG</a> builds the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Sprinter" title="Mercedes-Benz Sprinter">Mercedes-Benz Sprinter</a> light commercial vehicles in Düsseldorf. Since the 1960s, there has been a strong relationship between the city and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>. Many Japanese banks and corporations have their European headquarters in Düsseldorf – so many that Düsseldorf has the third largest Japanese community in Europe, after <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-virtualtourist.com_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-virtualtourist.com-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Japantag_in_D.C3.BCsseldorf:_Welcome_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Japantag_in_D.C3.BCsseldorf:_Welcome-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>The "Kö", which stands for <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsallee" title="Königsallee">Königsallee</a> ("King's Avenue"), is a popular shopping destination. Some of the most reputed jewellery shops, designer labels, and galleries have their stores here. The Kö has among the highest rents for retail and office space in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Important newspapers and journals such as <i><a href="/wiki/Handelsblatt" title="Handelsblatt">Handelsblatt</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rheinische_Post" title="Rheinische Post">Rheinische Post</a></i>, <i>Wirtschaftswoche</i>, <i>Deutsches Wirtschaftsblatt</i> and <i>VDI-Nachrichten</i> are published in Düsseldorf. Almost all of these papers are available online on the Internet. Renowned filmmaking companies, such as Germany's biggest cinema enterprise, the Riech-Group, and TV channels such as <a href="/wiki/Westdeutscher_Rundfunk" title="Westdeutscher Rundfunk">WDR</a> and <a href="/wiki/QVC" title="QVC">QVC</a> are located in Düsseldorf. The foundation <i>Film- und Medienstiftung NRW</i> is supporting the production of film and new media.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In regards to movies and movie theatres in Düsseldorf, movie goers have the option to choose between multiple different languages at the theatre. Many mainstream movies are shown in English, Spanish, French, and German.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport_DUS">Airport DUS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Airport DUS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Duesseldorf_international_terminal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Duesseldorf_international_terminal.jpg/220px-Duesseldorf_international_terminal.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Duesseldorf_international_terminal.jpg/330px-Duesseldorf_international_terminal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Duesseldorf_international_terminal.jpg/440px-Duesseldorf_international_terminal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Duesseldorf_international_terminal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Airport" title="Düsseldorf Airport">Düsseldorf Airport</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Airport" title="Düsseldorf Airport">Düsseldorf Airport</a>, also referred to as Rhein-Ruhr Airport, is located eight kilometres (5.0 miles) from the city centre and can easily be reached by train or the <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr_S-Bahn" title="Rhine-Ruhr S-Bahn">S-Bahn</a> urban railway. There is a <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Airport_station" title="Düsseldorf Airport station">long-distance train station</a> served by regional and national services, which is linked to the airport by the <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_SkyTrain" class="mw-redirect" title="Düsseldorf SkyTrain">SkyTrain</a>, an automatic <a href="/wiki/People_mover" title="People mover">people mover</a>. Another station situated under the terminal building carries the S-Bahn line (<a href="/wiki/S11_(Rhine-Ruhr_S-Bahn)" title="S11 (Rhine-Ruhr S-Bahn)">S11</a>) to <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Central_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Düsseldorf Central Station">Düsseldorf Central Station</a>, and to <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> as well as a few selected night services. After Frankfurt and Munich, Düsseldorf International is Germany's third largest <a href="/wiki/Airport" title="Airport">commercial airport</a>, with 21,850,489 passengers annually (2014). The airport offers 180 destinations on 4 continents, and is served by 70 airlines. The airport buildings were partly destroyed by a devastating fire caused by welding works in 1996, killing 17 people. It was completely rebuilt and the Skytrain installed.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway">Railway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Railway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:StadtbahnD.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/StadtbahnD.png/220px-StadtbahnD.png" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/StadtbahnD.png/330px-StadtbahnD.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/StadtbahnD.png/440px-StadtbahnD.png 2x" data-file-width="1544" data-file-height="2061" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:StadtbahnD.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Trams_in_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Trams in Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf Straßenbahn</a> and <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Stadtbahn" title="Düsseldorf Stadtbahn">Düsseldorf Stadtbahn</a> network, part of the <a href="/wiki/Verkehrsverbund_Rhein-Ruhr" title="Verkehrsverbund Rhein-Ruhr">Verkehrsverbund Rhein-Ruhr</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city is a major hub in the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> (DB) railway network. More than 1,000 trains stop in Düsseldorf daily. <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Central_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Düsseldorf Central Station">Düsseldorf Central Station</a> at Konrad-Adenauer-Platz is located in <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf-Stadtmitte" title="Düsseldorf-Stadtmitte">Düsseldorf-Stadtmitte</a>. Several <a href="/wiki/Rhein-Ruhr_S-Bahn" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhein-Ruhr S-Bahn">Rhein-Ruhr S-Bahn</a> lines connect Düsseldorf to other cities of <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr" title="Rhine-Ruhr">Rhine-Ruhr</a>. Local <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Trams in Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf Straßenbahn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Stadtbahn" title="Düsseldorf Stadtbahn">Düsseldorf Stadtbahn</a> traffic, as well as local bus traffic, is carried out by the city-owned <a href="/wiki/Rheinbahn" title="Rheinbahn">Rheinbahn</a> which operates within the <a href="/wiki/Verkehrsverbund_Rhein-Ruhr" title="Verkehrsverbund Rhein-Ruhr">VRR</a> <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">public transport</a> system. The light rail system also serves neighbouring cities and is partially operated underground. The Central Station and the Airport Station (Flughafen-Bahnhof) are connected to the national and <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Europe" title="High-speed rail in Europe">European high-speed systems</a> (Intercity/Eurocity, IC/EC and <a href="/wiki/InterCityExpress" class="mw-redirect" title="InterCityExpress">InterCityExpress</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxi">Taxi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Taxi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PKW_Mercedes_W210_P4297201.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/PKW_Mercedes_W210_P4297201.JPG/220px-PKW_Mercedes_W210_P4297201.JPG" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/PKW_Mercedes_W210_P4297201.JPG/330px-PKW_Mercedes_W210_P4297201.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/PKW_Mercedes_W210_P4297201.JPG/440px-PKW_Mercedes_W210_P4297201.JPG 2x" data-file-width="606" data-file-height="353" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PKW_Mercedes_W210_P4297201.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Officially licensed taxis are always ivory coloured</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Düsseldorf there are 1320 officially licensed Taxis. According to the regulations, the cars are always in ivory colour. On the back window you always find a black number on a yellow patch. Credit card payment has to be accepted at the Taxi stands at Airport of Düsseldorf. The supply of taxis in Düsseldorf is over the German average<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. Two taxi organisations cover the market<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. "Taxi-Düsseldorf" offers more than 1180 cabs in different sizes for max. 8 Passengers. The smaller one is "Rhein-Taxi" with more than 120 cabs. It is obligatory to carry out any journeys to destinations in the city and directly neighbouring cities.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Autobahn">Autobahn</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Autobahn">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>North Rhine-Westphalia has the densest network of <a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">autobahns</a> in Germany and Düsseldorf is directly accessible via the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_3" title="Bundesautobahn 3">A3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_44" title="Bundesautobahn 44">A44</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_46" title="Bundesautobahn 46">A46</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_52" title="Bundesautobahn 52">A52</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_57" title="Bundesautobahn 57">A57</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_59" title="Bundesautobahn 59">A59</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_524" title="Bundesautobahn 524">A524</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_recreation">Culture and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Culture and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(December 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Elector <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wilhelm,_Elector_Palatine" title="Johann Wilhelm, Elector Palatine">Jan Wellem</a> and his wife <a href="/wiki/Anna_Maria_Luisa_de%27_Medici" title="Anna Maria Luisa de' Medici">Anna Maria Luisa de' Medici</a> of Tuscany, were patrons of Düsseldorf's first significant cultural activities in the 17th and 18th centuries. <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Heine" title="Heinrich Heine">Heinrich Heine</a>, whose 200th birthday was celebrated in 1997 and who originally had a proposed <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Heine_Memorial" class="mw-redirect" title="Heinrich Heine Memorial">memorial</a> in the city dedicated to him; Clara and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Schumann" title="Robert Schumann">Robert Schumann</a>; and as <a href="/wiki/Felix_Mendelssohn" title="Felix Mendelssohn">Felix Mendelssohn</a>, are the most prominent artists related to the city, which is home to a distinguished <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Academy_of_Fine_Arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Düsseldorf Academy of Fine Arts">Academy of Fine Arts</a>.</p>
<p>The Düsseldorf cultural scene comprises traditional and <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a>, classical and glamorous. The world-famous state art collection of North Rhine-Westphalia, the highly acclaimed <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Oper_am_Rhein" title="Deutsche Oper am Rhein">Deutsche Oper am Rhein</a> (opera), and the <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorfer_Schauspielhaus" title="Düsseldorfer Schauspielhaus">Düsseldorfer Schauspielhaus</a> (theatre), artistic home of <a href="/wiki/Gustaf_Gr%C3%BCndgens" title="Gustaf Gründgens">Gustaf Gründgens</a>, are major elements of Düsseldorf's reputation as a centre of the fine arts.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beer">Beer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Beer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(December 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Düsseldorf is well known for its <a href="/wiki/Altbier" title="Altbier">Altbier</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> a hoppy beer which translates as <i>old [style] beer</i>, a reference to the pre-<a href="/wiki/Lager" title="Lager">lager</a> brewing method of using a warm <a href="/wiki/Top-fermenting_yeast" class="mw-redirect" title="Top-fermenting yeast">top-fermenting yeast</a> like British pale ales.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Over time the Alt yeast adjusted to lower temperatures, and the Alt brewers would store or lager the beer after fermentation, leading to a cleaner, crisper beer. The name "altbier" first appeared in the 19th century to differentiate the beers of Düsseldorf from the new <a href="/wiki/Pale_lager" title="Pale lager">pale lager</a> that was gaining a hold on Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brewers in Düsseldorf used the pale malts that were used for the modern pale lagers, but retained the old ("alt") method of using warm fermenting yeasts. The first brewery to use the name Alt was Schumacher which opened in 1838.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The founder, Mathias Schumacher, allowed the beer to mature in cool conditions in wooden casks for longer than normal, and laid the foundation for the modern alt – amber coloured and lagered.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The result is a pale beer that has some of the lean dryness of a lager but with fruity notes as well.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are five pub-breweries in Düsseldorf which brew Altbier on the premises: Füchschen, Schumacher, Schlüssel, Uerige and Brauerei Kürzer. Four of the five are in the historic centre of Düsseldorf (Altstadt); the other (Schumacher), between the Altstadt and Düsseldorf Central railway station (Hauptbahnhof), also maintains an establishment in the Altstadt, Im Goldenen Kessel, across the street from Schlüssel.</p>
<p>Each (except Brauerei Kürzer) produces a special, secret, seasonal "Sticke" version in small quantities, though the names vary: Schlüssel spells it "Stike", without the "c", while Schumacher calls its special beer "Latzenbier", meaning "slat beer", possibly because the kegs from which it was poured had been stored on raised shelves.<sup id="cite_ref-Dornbusch_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dornbusch-31">[31]</a></sup> Füchschen's seasonal is its Weihnachtsbier (Christmas beer), available in bottles starting mid-November, and served in the brewpub on <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Eve" title="Christmas Eve">Christmas Eve</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fuchschen_Weihnachtsbier_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fuchschen_Weihnachtsbier-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_nightlife">Music and nightlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Music and nightlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sensation_White_2008_Silvester_-_LTU_Arena,_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Sensation_White_2008_Silvester_-_LTU_Arena%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/220px-Sensation_White_2008_Silvester_-_LTU_Arena%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Sensation_White_2008_Silvester_-_LTU_Arena%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/330px-Sensation_White_2008_Silvester_-_LTU_Arena%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Sensation_White_2008_Silvester_-_LTU_Arena%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/440px-Sensation_White_2008_Silvester_-_LTU_Arena%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sensation_White_2008_Silvester_-_LTU_Arena,_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sensation_White" class="mw-redirect" title="Sensation White">Sensation White</a> New Year's Eve party, <a href="/wiki/Esprit_Arena" title="Esprit Arena">Esprit Arena</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since the 1950s the "<a href="/wiki/Kom(m)%C3%B6dchen" title="Kom(m)ödchen">Kom(m)ödchen</a>" has been one of the most prominent political cabarets of Germany. The city's most famous contribution to the culture of modern <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">popular music</a> is beyond doubt the avant-garde <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic music</a> band <a href="/wiki/Kraftwerk" title="Kraftwerk">Kraftwerk</a>. Formed by a few Düsseldorf-born musicians, <a href="/wiki/Kraftwerk" title="Kraftwerk">Kraftwerk</a> are internationally known as the most significant band in the history of <a href="/wiki/Post-war" title="Post-war">post-war</a> <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Germany" title="Music of Germany">German music</a> and as pioneers in electronic music.<sup id="cite_ref-graun_kraftwerk_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-graun_kraftwerk-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Internationally known <a href="/wiki/Power_metal" title="Power metal">power metal</a> band <a href="/wiki/Warlock_(band)" title="Warlock (band)">Warlock</a> was formed in Düsseldorf in 1982. Their frontwoman, <a href="/wiki/Doro_(musician)" title="Doro (musician)">Doro Pesch</a>, has had a successful solo career in Europe and Asia since <a href="/wiki/Warlock_(band)" title="Warlock (band)">Warlock</a> ended. The <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk band</a> <a href="/wiki/Die_Toten_Hosen" title="Die Toten Hosen">Die Toten Hosen</a>, which is famous around the world, also the most popular singers<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> in Germany <a href="/wiki/Westernhagen" class="mw-redirect" title="Westernhagen">Westernhagen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heino" title="Heino">Heino</a> come from Düsseldorf. The electronic act <a href="/wiki/Deutsch_Amerikanische_Freundschaft" title="Deutsch Amerikanische Freundschaft">D.A.F.</a> was formed in the city in 1978, as well as the electronic/industrial pioneers <a href="/wiki/Die_Krupps" title="Die Krupps">Die Krupps</a> in 1980. The experimental <a href="/wiki/Post-punk" title="Post-punk">post-punk</a> group <a href="/wiki/La_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="La Düsseldorf">La Düsseldorf</a> was named after the city, for which it paid with a legal case in the early 1980s. Another famous formation is <a href="/wiki/Fehlfarben" title="Fehlfarben">Fehlfarben</a>. Founded in the late 1970s by Peter Hein, Frank Fenstermacher, Kurt Dahlke and Michael Kemner.</p>
<p>Düsseldorf appears is several songs, including <i>Düsseldorf</i> by the British indie band <a href="/wiki/Teleman" title="Teleman">Teleman</a> and <i>Wärst du doch in Düsseldorf geblieben</i> by Danish singer <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorthe_Kollo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dorthe Kollo (page does not exist)">Dorthe Kollo</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion">Fashion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Fashion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Düsseldorf, Germany is the <a href="/wiki/Fashion" title="Fashion">fashion</a> capital of Germany as it is a major cultural center for the art and fashion scenes. The fashionable clothes trend took root in this city before 1949. 1949 is the date of the first fashion show staged in Düsseldorf. Fashion trends have occurred as access to more elegant clothing for the general public has been a part of the culture for almost a century. Two times a year an event called the, “Voices of Fashion,” occurs and attracts many people to visit Düsseldorf to find the latest fashion items. There are famous designers that have made a name for themselves in Düsseldorf as well. Designers Sabine Schumacher, Peter O. Mahler, and Renate Harvan all design in Düsseldorf. To keep the creativity and passion for fashion alive in Düsseldorf everyday there are schools dedicated to fashion design in Düsseldorf as well. Akademie Mode and Design Institution, Design Department Academy, and Mode Design College are the three prominent fashion schools residing in Düsseldorf.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Carnival">Carnival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Carnival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Carnival_in_Germany,_Switzerland_and_Austria#Rhineland" title="Carnival in Germany, Switzerland and Austria">Carnival in Germany, Switzerland and Austria §&#160;Rhineland</a></div>
<p>One of the biggest cultural events in Düsseldorf is the <i><a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">Karneval</a></i> (also referred to as the "fifth season") which starts every year on 11 November at 11:11&#160;a.m., and reaches its climax on <i><a href="/wiki/Rosenmontag" title="Rosenmontag">Rosenmontag</a></i> (Rose Monday), featuring a huge parade through the streets of Düsseldorf. <i>Karneval</i> ends on <i>Aschermittwoch</i> (<a href="/wiki/Ash_Wednesday" title="Ash Wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>).</p>
<h3><span id="Cartwheeler_of_Düsseldorf"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cartwheeler_of_D.C3.BCsseldorf">Cartwheeler of Düsseldorf</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cartwheeler of Düsseldorf">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf%27s_cartwheeler" title="Düsseldorf's cartwheeler">Düsseldorf's cartwheeler</a></div>
<p>The <i>Düsseldorfer Radschläger</i> (<i>Boy who does <a href="/wiki/Cartwheel_(gymnastics)" title="Cartwheel (gymnastics)">Cartwheels</a></i>) is said to be the city's oldest tradition. The symbol of the cartwheeler can be found on many souvenirs and various things in Düsseldorf have the cartwheelers to thank for their names. This tradition was honoured in 1954 by the erection of a fountain, called Cartwheeler's Fountain, on the <i>Burgplatz</i> in Düsseldorf.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Legends_of_its_origin_and_history">Legends of its origin and history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Legends of its origin and history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(December 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The tradition cannot be linked to one specific historical event, instead, there are several stories surrounding the beginnings of the Düsseldorf Cartwheelers. Probably the most well known version is <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Worringen" title="Battle of Worringen">Battle of Worringen</a>. In the battle of 1288 <a href="/wiki/Adolf_VIII_of_Berg" title="Adolf VIII of Berg">Count Adolf</a> devastatingly defeated the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">Archbishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>. As a consequence of this victory, Düsseldorf obtained <a href="/wiki/Town_privileges" title="Town privileges">Town privileges</a>. The inhabitants, especially the children ran joyfully on the streets and performed <a href="/wiki/Cartwheel_(gymnastics)" title="Cartwheel (gymnastics)">cartwheels</a>.</p>
<p>Another story talks about a wedding procession during which one of the wheels of the wedding carriage broke. In order to fend off the threat of bad luck, a boy supposedly jumped to the carriage, took hold of the wheel and thus became a living part of the wheel. Whether the story is about the marriage of <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wilhelm,_Elector_Palatine" title="Johann Wilhelm, Elector Palatine">Jan Wellem</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anna_Maria_Luisa_de%27_Medici" title="Anna Maria Luisa de' Medici">Anna Maria Luisa de' Medici</a> or the wedding of Margravine <a href="/wiki/Jakobea_of_Baden" title="Jakobea of Baden">Jakobea of Baden</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_William,_Duke_of_J%C3%BClich-Cleves-Berg" title="John William, Duke of Jülich-Cleves-Berg">Johann Wilhelm</a> is debatable.</p>
<p>Another story gives an account of this wedding between Margrave Jacobe von Baden and Johann Wilhelm, in 1585. According to legend she felt miserable about her marriage, but the cartwheelers who displayed their skills next to her carriage were able to make her smile. Numerous travelers were attracted to the city by great exhibitions - the forerunner of today’s fairs - between the end of the 19th century and the beginning of the 20th century. During this time the children who did the cart wheeling found out that it was a profitable source of income. The bourgeoisie accepted this in good humour as a symbolic act of local patriotism. In the beginning the lads shouted <i>"för eene Penning schlage ich das Rad“</i> (cartwheel for a penny). The Jan Wellem monument returned to Düsseldorf at the end of the Second World War. The procession was accompanied by torches, fanfares and the cartwheeling boys.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Cartwheelers_in_the_cityscape">Cartwheelers in the cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Cartwheelers in the cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Cartwheelers can be found by several fountains within the city. The most famous is Cartwheeler’s Fountain in <i>Burgplatz</i> with an inscription of a quote by Hans Müller-Schlösser: "<i>Radschläger wolle mer blieve, wie jeck et de Minschen och drieve“</i> (We will always remain cartwheelers, however crazy it drives people.) The fountain was designed by Alfred Zschorsch in 1954 and donated by the <i>Heimatverein Düsseldorfer Jonges</i>, which is a club devoted to the maintenance of local and regional traditions. There are other cartwheelers that decorate storm drains and the door knocker on the Church of Lambertus, which was designed by Friedrich Becker. He created the cartwheeler in front of the Schadow Arcades.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>This tradition has been kept alive by the <i>Alde Düsseldorfer Bürgergesellschaft von 1920 e. V.</i>, a society founded in 1920, who organized the first cartwheeler competition on 17 October 1937. Since 1971 this event has been held annually<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> in cooperation with the <i>Stadtsparkasse</i> (a local bank), but formerly took place in the <i><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsallee" title="Königsallee">Königsallee</a></i>. Since 2006 it has taken place on the <i>Rheinwerft</i>, near the old part of town. This is a fixed date in the city’s calendar of events. About 500 boys regularly participate in this event and since 1971 girls have also taken part. In 2001 the art project <i>Radschläger-Kunst</i> (Cartwheeler Art) was called into life, in which over 100 cartwheeler sculptures have been designed by various artists. The door knocker on the Church of Lambertus functioned as a model for the sculptures that are 2 metres (6&#160;feet 7&#160;inches) high, 2 metres (6&#160;feet 7&#160;inches) wide and 30&#160;cm (12&#160;in) deep. They were positioned around the city centre. Some of the sculptures have been auctioned off to companies and private owners.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christmas_Market">Christmas Market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Christmas Market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Every <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a>, the city of Düsseldorf uses the city centre to host one of the largest Christmas gatherings in Germany. The Christmas festival occurs every year from 17 November until 23 December. This Christmas fest brings Düsseldorf a large portion of tourism every year as many people from nearby areas come to the city to drink <a href="/wiki/Mulled_wine" title="Mulled wine">mulled wine</a> and hot chocolate and watch craftsman <a href="/wiki/Glassblowing" title="Glassblowing">blow glass</a> and create art. The event contains many small wooden buildings all clustered in the middle of the city for all the citizens to enjoy. The event, to many visitors, has an old European feel, but is very lively.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Traditional meals in the region are Rheinischer <a href="/wiki/Sauerbraten" title="Sauerbraten">Sauerbraten</a> (a beef roast and sometimes horse marinated for a few days in vinegar and spices served with gravy and raisins) and <a href="/wiki/Himmel_und_erde" class="mw-redirect" title="Himmel und erde">Heaven and Earth</a> (Himmel und Äd; <a href="/wiki/Black_pudding" title="Black pudding">black pudding</a> with stewed apples mixed with <a href="/wiki/Mashed_potato" title="Mashed potato">mashed potatoes</a>). In winter the people like to eat Muscheln Rheinischer Art (Rhenish-style mussels) as well as <a href="/wiki/Reibekuchen" title="Reibekuchen">Reibekuchen</a> (fried potato pancake served with apple sauce). Also a special meal: Düsseldorfer Senfrostbraten (Steaks roasted with Düsseldorf mustard on top).</p>
<p>Düsseldorf is known for its strong <a href="/wiki/Dijon_mustard" title="Dijon mustard">Dijon</a>-like <a href="/wiki/Mustard_(condiment)" title="Mustard (condiment)">mustard</a> served in a traditional pot called "Mostertpöttche", which was eternalised in a <a href="/wiki/Still_life" title="Still life">still life</a> by <a href="/wiki/Vincent_van_Gogh" title="Vincent van Gogh">Vincent van Gogh</a> in 1884.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Rhine Metropolis is one of the most diverse areas in terms of culinary diversity. Düsseldorf, with the third largest Japanese community in Europe, not only provides a wide range of culinary cuisine but also has a solid foundation of Authentic Asian food in the city. Düsseldorf’s exceptional culinary cuisine has been recognized and visited by the Worldwide leading travel guide of Lonely Planet. Along with a broad range of diverse cultural cuisine, Düsseldorf is also home to various Michelin starred restaurants that are world renowned.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p><b>Alve Hahn</b> - this dish is made from a half a double rye roll, which is another of the specialties of Düsseldorf, buttered, with a thick slice of aged Gouda cheese, onions, mustard, ground paprika and sour pickles.</p>
<p><b>Himmel un Aad</b> - a dish of mashed potatoes and apples along with slices of blutwurst. Caramelized onions are usually served with this meal.</p>
<p><b>Reibekuchen</b> is another famous dish from Düsseldorf; this dish is usually drizzled with Rübensyrup (beet syrup) and is served on pumpernickel slices along with applesauce<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/F%C3%B6rderpreis_f%C3%BCr_Literatur_der_Landeshauptstadt_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Förderpreis für Literatur der Landeshauptstadt Düsseldorf">Förderpreis für Literatur der Landeshauptstadt Düsseldorf</a></i> is a German <a href="/wiki/Literary_award" title="Literary award">Literary award</a> donated by the City of Düsseldorf in <a href="/wiki/Northrhine-Westphalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Northrhine-Westphalia">Northrhine-Westphalia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The Prize for Literature in support of the City of Düsseldorf is awarded since 1972 by the Council of the City due to the decisions of the courts.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Förderpreis für Literatur der Landeshauptstadt Düsseldorf</i> is given once a year to artists and groups, especially to the areas of poetry, writing, review and translation.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalry_with_Cologne">Rivalry with Cologne</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Rivalry with Cologne">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Düsseldorf and <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> have a "fierce regional rivalry".<sup id="cite_ref-Rivalry_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rivalry-42">[42]</a></sup> The rivalry includes <a href="/wiki/Carnival_in_Germany,_Switzerland_and_Austria" title="Carnival in Germany, Switzerland and Austria">carnival</a> parades, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Association_ice_hockey&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Association ice hockey (page does not exist)">ice hockey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rivalry_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rivalry-42">[42]</a></sup> People in Cologne prefer <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6lsch_(beer)" title="Kölsch (beer)">Kölsch</a> while people in Düsseldorf prefer Alt.<sup id="cite_ref-Rivalry_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rivalry-42">[42]</a></sup> Waiters and patrons will "scorn" and make a "mockery" of people who order Alt beer in Cologne and Kölsch in Düsseldorf.<sup id="cite_ref-Rivalry_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rivalry-42">[42]</a></sup> The rivalry has been described as a "love-hate relationship".<sup id="cite_ref-Rivalry_42-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rivalry-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatres">Theatres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Theatres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span id="Museums,_arts_and_history_institutes,_and_other_attractions"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums.2C_arts_and_history_institutes.2C_and_other_attractions">Museums, arts and history institutes, and other attractions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Museums, arts and history institutes, and other attractions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Düsseldorf's <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team <a href="/wiki/Fortuna_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Fortuna Düsseldorf">Fortuna Düsseldorf</a> won the 1933 German championship, the <a href="/wiki/German_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="German Cup">German Cup</a> in 1979 and 1980, and were finalists in the <a href="/wiki/European_Cup_Winners_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="European Cup Winners Cup">European Cup Winners Cup</a> in 1979. After 15 years in lower leagues they were promoted following a play-off win over <a href="/wiki/Hertha_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Hertha Berlin">Hertha Berlin</a> in 2012. As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, they are back in the second division of German soccer. Their new stadium, the <a href="/wiki/Esprit_Arena" title="Esprit Arena">Esprit arena</a>, opened in January 2005 and has a capacity of 54,500. Düsseldorf was one of nine host cities for the <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974 FIFA World Cup</a>, and the Rochusclub Düsseldorf has hosted the tennis <a href="/wiki/World_Team_Cup" title="World Team Cup">World Team Cup</a> from 1978 till 2012.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Düsseldorf also held the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Tour_de_France_Grands_D%C3%A9parts" title="List of Tour de France Grands Départs">Grand Départ</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2017_Tour_de_France" title="2017 Tour de France">Tour de France</a> in July 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other sports in Düsseldorf are <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> (the <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorfer_EG" title="Düsseldorfer EG">Düsseldorfer EG</a> which play in the new <a href="/wiki/ISS-Dome" class="mw-redirect" title="ISS-Dome">ISS-Dome</a>) and <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a>. The <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Panther" title="Düsseldorf Panther">Düsseldorf Panther</a> are one of the most successful teams in Germany with six <a href="/wiki/German_Bowl" title="German Bowl">German Bowl</a> titles and the <a href="/wiki/Eurobowl" title="Eurobowl">Eurobowl</a> victory in 1995. In addition the Junior-Team is the most successful youth department in Germany with fifteen <a href="/wiki/German_Junior_Bowl" title="German Junior Bowl">Junior Bowl</a> victories. <a href="/wiki/Rhein_Fire" title="Rhein Fire">Rhine Fire Düsseldorf</a> was an established team of the <a href="/wiki/NFL_Europa" class="mw-redirect" title="NFL Europa">NFL Europe</a> and won the <a href="/wiki/World_Bowl" title="World Bowl">World Bowl</a> two times in 1998 and 2000. Düsseldorf has a successful <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> team (Düsseldorf Dragons), who play in the regional NRW league and consistently finish with a top-three position.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Table_tennis" title="Table tennis">Table tennis</a> is also played (Borussia Düsseldorf – the most successful team in Germany with <a href="/wiki/Timo_Boll" title="Timo Boll">Timo Boll</a>), as are <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">handball</a> (HSG Düsseldorf), <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gloria_Giants_D%C3%BCsseldorf" class="mw-redirect" title="Gloria Giants Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf Giants</a>), <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> (Düsseldorf Senators) and <a href="/wiki/Dance" title="Dance">dancing</a> (Rot-Weiß Düsseldorf). Düsseldorf also has a <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> team, the Düsseldorf Blackcaps, who play in the regional NRW league.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/University_of_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="University of Düsseldorf">Heinrich Heine University</a> Düsseldorf is located in the southern part of the city. It has about 20,000 students and a wide range of subjects in <a href="/wiki/Natural_science" title="Natural science">natural sciences</a>, mathematics, <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer sciences</a>, philosophy, <a href="/wiki/Social_sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Social sciences">social sciences</a>, arts, languages, medicine, pharmacy, economy and the law.</p>
<p>Other academic institutions include</p>
<ul>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Clara_Schumann" title="Clara Schumann">Clara Schumann</a> Musikschule (music school)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Robert_Schumann_Hochschule" title="Robert Schumann Hochschule">Robert Schumann Hochschule</a></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Kunstakademie_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Kunstakademie Düsseldorf">Kunstakademie Düsseldorf</a><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> (Academy of <a href="/wiki/Fine_art" title="Fine art">Fine Arts</a>) which is famous for high-profile artists like Joseph Beuys, Paul Klee, Nam June Paik, Gerhard Richter, the Bechers, and Andreas Gursky</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Hochschule_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Hochschule Düsseldorf">Hochschule Düsseldorf</a><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> (University of <a href="/wiki/Applied_science" title="Applied science">Applied Sciences</a>)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/AMD_Academy_of_Fashion_and_Design" title="AMD Academy of Fashion and Design">AMD Academy of Fashion and Design</a><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Iron_Research_GmbH" class="mw-redirect" title="Max Planck Institute for Iron Research GmbH">Max Planck Institute for Iron Research</a><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Goethe-Institut" title="Goethe-Institut">Goethe Institute</a><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></li>
<li>Verwaltungs- und Wirtschafts-Akademie Düsseldorf</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WHU-Otto_Beisheim_School_of_Management" title="WHU-Otto Beisheim School of Management">WHU-Otto Beisheim School of Management</a> (Düsseldorf Campus)</li>
</ul>
<p>International primary and secondary schools:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_School_of_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="International School of Düsseldorf">International School of Düsseldorf</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lyc%C3%A9e_fran%C3%A7ais_de_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Lycée français de Düsseldorf">Lycée français de Düsseldorf</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Japanische_Internationale_Schule_in_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Japanische Internationale Schule in Düsseldorf">Japanische Internationale Schule in Düsseldorf</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_buildings">Notable buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Notable buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%BCsseldorf,_Medienhafen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/D%C3%BCsseldorf%2C_Medienhafen.jpg/220px-D%C3%BCsseldorf%2C_Medienhafen.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/D%C3%BCsseldorf%2C_Medienhafen.jpg/330px-D%C3%BCsseldorf%2C_Medienhafen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/D%C3%BCsseldorf%2C_Medienhafen.jpg/440px-D%C3%BCsseldorf%2C_Medienhafen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%BCsseldorf,_Medienhafen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i><a href="/wiki/Neuer_Zollhof" title="Neuer Zollhof">Neuer Zollhof</a></i> at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Medienhafen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Medienhafen (page does not exist)">Medienhafen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rheinturm_D%C3%BCsseldorf" class="mw-redirect" title="Rheinturm Düsseldorf">Rheinturm</a> (TV tower) the city's landmark (1982: 234&#160;m [&#160;768&#160;ft&#160;], since 2004: 240.50&#160;m [&#160;789.0&#160;ft&#160;]), the lights on which comprise the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Digital_clock" title="Digital clock">digital clock</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Frank_Gehry" title="Frank Gehry">Gehry</a> buildings in the Düsseldorf media harbour (see picture above).</li>
<li>The Colorium, an 18-storey tower designed by Alsop and Partners, also in the Düsseldorf media harbour.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Schloss_Benrath" title="Schloss Benrath">Benrather Schloss</a> (Benrath palace).</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Grupello-Haus" title="Grupello-Haus">Grupello-Haus</a> probably designed by the Italian architect <a href="/w/index.php?title=Matteo_Alberti_(architect)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Matteo Alberti (architect) (page does not exist)">Matteo Alberti</a> in 1706 for Duke <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wilhelm,_Elector_Palatine" title="Johann Wilhelm, Elector Palatine">Johann Wilhelm</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Wilhem_Marx_House" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilhem Marx House">Wilhem Marx House</a> of 1922/24: at twelve storeys high, it was Germany's first <a href="/wiki/Skyscraper" title="Skyscraper">high-rise building</a>.</li>
<li>The Stahlhof of 1906, the administrative centre of Germany's steel economy until 1945.</li>
<li>The Stummhaus of 1925, another early German high-rise building.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gerresheim_Basilica&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gerresheim Basilica (page does not exist)">Gerresheim Basilica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Suitbertus_Basilica&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="St Suitbertus Basilica (page does not exist)">St Suitbertus Basilica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>DRV Tower, 120-metre-high (394&#160;ft) tower constructed in 1978.</li>
<li>GAP 15, an 85-metre-high (279&#160;ft) building constructed in 2005 near <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsallee" title="Königsallee">Königsallee</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ARAG-Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="ARAG-Tower">ARAG-Tower</a>, at 131&#160;m (430&#160;ft) in height, it is Düsseldorf's highest <a href="/wiki/Office" title="Office">office building</a>; designed by <a href="/wiki/Sir_Norman_Foster" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Norman Foster">Sir Norman Foster</a>.</li>
<li>Eight bridges span the Rhine at Düsseldorf; they, too, are city landmarks.</li>
<li>Eastern pylon of <a href="/wiki/Reisholz_Rhine_Powerline_Crossing" title="Reisholz Rhine Powerline Crossing">Reisholz Rhine Powerline Crossing</a>, an electricity pylon under whose legs runs a rail.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_places">Notable places</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Notable places">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>Kö (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsallee" title="Königsallee">Königsallee</a>), a shopping street with luxuries shops</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Schloss_Benrath" title="Schloss Benrath">Schloss Benrath</a>, rococo castle</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Altstadt_(D%C3%BCsseldorf)" title="Altstadt (Düsseldorf)">Altstadt (Düsseldorf)</a>, literally "old town", the historic town centre. Nowadays Düsseldorf's entertainment district with hundreds of pubs and restaurants, and proverbially known by Germans as "the longest bar in the world".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf-Hafen" title="Düsseldorf-Hafen">Düsseldorf-Hafen</a>, the harbour is a modern build district</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kaiserswerth" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaiserswerth">Kaiserswerth</a>, historical district with the ruined castle of Barbarossa <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick I, Holy Roman Emperor">Frederick I, Holy Roman Emperor</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hofgarten,_D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hofgarten, Düsseldorf (page does not exist)">Hofgarten</a>, old city park</li>
</ul>
<h2><span id="Twin_towns_–_sister_cities"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities">Twin towns – sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Twin towns – sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Germany" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany">List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany</a></div>

<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/China" title="China"><img alt="China" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a>, China<sup id="cite_ref-FC_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FC-63">[63]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel"><img alt="Israel" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/21px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png" width="21" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/32px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/41px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="660" data-file-height="480" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa</a>, Israel<sup id="cite_ref-FC_63-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FC-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Haifa_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haifa-64">[64]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia"><img alt="Russia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, Russia<sup id="cite_ref-FC_63-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FC-63">[63]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom"><img alt="United Kingdom" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Reading,_Berkshire" title="Reading, Berkshire">Reading</a>, UK, since 1947, officially since 1988<sup id="cite_ref-FC_63-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FC-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reading_twinning_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reading_twinning-65">[65]</a></sup></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_Natives">Notable Natives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Notable Natives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Born_before_1850">Born before 1850</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Born before 1850">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heinrich_Heine-Oppenheim.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Heinrich_Heine-Oppenheim.jpg/130px-Heinrich_Heine-Oppenheim.jpg" width="130" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Heinrich_Heine-Oppenheim.jpg/195px-Heinrich_Heine-Oppenheim.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Heinrich_Heine-Oppenheim.jpg/260px-Heinrich_Heine-Oppenheim.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1445" data-file-height="1832" /></a>

<div class="thumb tright">
