<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois-Charles_de_Velbr%C3%BCck" title="François-Charles de Velbrück">François-Charles de Velbrück</a>, (1719–1784), Prince-Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge" title="Liège">Liège</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Helena_Curtens" title="Helena Curtens">Helena Curtens</a>, (1722–1738), last victim of the witch trials in the Lower Rhine</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Johann_Georg_Jacobi" title="Johann Georg Jacobi">Johann Georg Jacobi</a>, (1740–1814), writer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Heinrich_Jacobi" title="Friedrich Heinrich Jacobi">Friedrich Heinrich Jacobi</a>, (1743–1819), philosopher and writer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peter_von_Cornelius" title="Peter von Cornelius">Peter von Cornelius</a>, (1783–1867), painter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Heine" title="Heinrich Heine">Heinrich Heine</a>, (1797–1856), poet and writer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_von_Hatzfeldt" title="Paul von Hatzfeldt">Paul Graf von Hatzfeld to Trachenberg</a>, (1851–1901), Secretary of State and head of the Foreign Office of the German Reich 1881–1885</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eugen_Richter" title="Eugen Richter">Eugen Richter</a>, (1838–1906), today part of Berlin, politician and publicist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arnold_Forstmann" title="Arnold Forstmann">Arnold Forstmann</a>, (1842–1914), landscape painter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peter_Janssen" title="Peter Janssen">Peter Janssen</a>, (1844–1908), painter, professor at the Art Academy</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Born_1851–1900"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Born_1851.E2.80.931900">Born 1851–1900</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Born 1851–1900">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Georg_Wenker_Georg_Wenker_(1852-1911)_(Alter_Fritz).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Georg_Wenker_Georg_Wenker_%281852-1911%29_%28Alter_Fritz%29.jpg/150px-Georg_Wenker_Georg_Wenker_%281852-1911%29_%28Alter_Fritz%29.jpg" width="150" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/24/Georg_Wenker_Georg_Wenker_%281852-1911%29_%28Alter_Fritz%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="207" data-file-height="285" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Georg_Wenker_Georg_Wenker_(1852-1911)_(Alter_Fritz).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Georg Wenker</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Georg_Wenker" title="Georg Wenker">Georg Wenker</a>, (1852–1911), linguist, founder of linguistic atlas of the German Reich (Wenkeratlas)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Karl_Janssen" title="Karl Janssen">Karl Janssen</a>, (1855–1927), sculptor, professor at the Art Academy</li>
<li>Fritz Reiss, (1857–1915), lithographer, illustrator, graphic artist and painter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bruno_Schmitz" title="Bruno Schmitz">Bruno Schmitz</a>, (1858–1916), architect</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Otto_Hupp" title="Otto Hupp">Otto Hupp</a>, (1859–1949), signature graphic artist, engraver</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Albert_Herzfeld" title="Albert Herzfeld">Albert Herzfeld</a>, (1865–1943), painter and author</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hanns_Heinz_Ewers" title="Hanns Heinz Ewers">Hanns Heinz Ewers</a>, (1871–1943), writer and filmmaker</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Levison" title="Wilhelm Levison">Wilhelm Levison</a>, (1876–1947), historian</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elly_Ney" title="Elly Ney">Elly Ney</a>, (1882–1968), world-famous concert pianist</li>
<li>Carl Maria Weber, (1890–1953), writer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Willy_Reetz" title="Willy Reetz">Willy Reetz</a>, (1892–1963), painter, "Düsseldorf School"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hermann_Kn%C3%BCfken" title="Hermann Knüfken">Hermann Knüfken</a>, (1893–1976), marine soldier, revolutionary, union activist, resistance fighter and secret agent</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Gehre" title="Ludwig Gehre">Ludwig Gehre</a>, (1895–1945) in <a href="/wiki/Flossenb%C3%BCrg" title="Flossenbürg">Flossenbürg</a>, officer and resistance fighter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hans_Globke" title="Hans Globke">Hans Globke</a>, (1898–1973), jurist, National Socialist, from 1949 Assistant Secretary, then Secretary of State in the Federal Chancellery (1953–1963)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Karl_von_Appen" title="Karl von Appen">Karl von Appen</a>, (1900–1981), stage designer</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Born_after_1900">Born after 1900</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Born after 1900">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anefo_910-9501_Filmregisseur.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Anefo_910-9501_Filmregisseur.jpg/150px-Anefo_910-9501_Filmregisseur.jpg" width="150" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Anefo_910-9501_Filmregisseur.jpg/225px-Anefo_910-9501_Filmregisseur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Anefo_910-9501_Filmregisseur.jpg/300px-Anefo_910-9501_Filmregisseur.jpg 2x" data-file-width="839" data-file-height="1280" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anefo_910-9501_Filmregisseur.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Helmut Käutner 1960</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jacob_Sporrenberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Jacob Sporrenberg">Jacob Sporrenberg</a>, (1902–1952, SS-group leader, lieutenant general of police and politician (NSDAP)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Toni_Ulmen" title="Toni Ulmen">Toni Ulmen</a>, (1906–1976), motorcycle and car race driver</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Helmut_K%C3%A4utner" title="Helmut Käutner">Helmut Käutner</a>, (1908–1980), film director („<a href="/wiki/Des_Teufels_General" title="Des Teufels General">Des Teufels General</a>“, „<a href="/wiki/Das_Haus_in_Montevideo_(1963)" class="mw-redirect" title="Das Haus in Montevideo (1963)">Das Haus in Montevideo</a>“), actor</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hilarius_Gilges" title="Hilarius Gilges">Hilarius Gilges</a>, (1909–1933), Afro-German actor, victim of National Socialism</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Habermas" title="Jürgen Habermas">Jürgen Habermas</a>, (born 1929), famous philosopher and sociologist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wim_Wenders" title="Wim Wenders">Wim Wenders</a>, (born 1945), filmmaker, playwright, author</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marius_M%C3%BCller-Westernhagen" title="Marius Müller-Westernhagen">Marius Müller-Westernhagen</a>, (born 1948), actor and musician</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andreas_Gursky" title="Andreas Gursky">Andreas Gursky</a>, (born 1955), photographer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bettina_B%C3%B6ttinger" title="Bettina Böttinger">Bettina Böttinger</a>, (born 1956), TV-presenter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Birgitt_Bender" title="Birgitt Bender">Birgitt Bender</a>, (born 1956), politician (The Greens), Member of Landtag and Bundestag</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andreas_Frege" class="mw-redirect" title="Andreas Frege">Andreas Frege</a>, (born 1962), „Campino“, singer in the band <a href="/wiki/Die_Toten_Hosen" title="Die Toten Hosen">Die Toten Hosen</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Obermann" title="René Obermann">René Obermann</a>, (born 1963), manager, husband of <a href="/wiki/Maybrit_Illner" title="Maybrit Illner">Maybrit Illner</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Preetz" title="Michael Preetz">Michael Preetz</a>, (born 1967), former football-player</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heike_Makatsch" title="Heike Makatsch">Heike Makatsch</a>, (born 1971), actress and singer</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="The_following_figures_are_not_natives_of_the_city,_but_have_a_connection_to_Düsseldorf:"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_following_figures_are_not_natives_of_the_city.2C_but_have_a_connection_to_D.C3.BCsseldorf:">The following figures are not natives of the city, but have a connection to Düsseldorf:</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=D%C3%BCsseldorf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: The following figures are not natives of the city, but have a connection to Düsseldorf:">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/William_Thomas_Mulvany" title="William Thomas Mulvany">William Thomas Mulvany</a>, * 1806 <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, † October 30, 1885 in Düsseldorf, entrepreneur</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Schumann" title="Robert Schumann">Robert Schumann</a>, born June 8, 1810 in <a href="/wiki/Zwickau" title="Zwickau">Zwickau</a>, † July 29, 1856 in Endenich, composer, 1850–1854 urban music director in Düsseldorf</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alfred_Rethel" title="Alfred Rethel">Alfred Rethel</a>, born May 5, 1816 in <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a>; † December 1, 1859 in Düsseldorf, history painter</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ernestine_Friedrichsen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ernestine Friedrichsen (page does not exist)">Ernestine Friedrichsen</a> * June 29, 1824 in <a href="/wiki/Danzig" class="mw-redirect" title="Danzig">Danzig</a>; † July 21, 1892 in Düsseldorf, genre painter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clara_Schumann" title="Clara Schumann">Clara Schumann</a>, born September 13, 1819 in <a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a>, † May 20, 1896 in Frankfurt am Main; pianist and composer, wife of Robert Schumann, frequent host of <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Brahms" title="Johannes Brahms">Johannes Brahms</a> in Düsseldorf (1850–1854)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Emanuel_Leutze" title="Emanuel Leutze">Emanuel Leutze</a>, born May 24, 1824 in <a href="/wiki/Schw%C3%A4bisch_Gm%C3%BCnd" title="Schwäbisch Gmünd">Schwäbisch Gmünd</a>, † July 18, 1868 in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_DC" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington, DC">Washington, DC</a>, painter, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Düsseldorf School">Düsseldorf School</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Louise_Dumont" title="Louise Dumont">Louise Dumont</a>, born February 22, 1862 in <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>; † 16 May 1932 in Düsseldorf, actress and 1904 founder of the <i>Schauspielhaus Düsseldorf</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Johanna_Ey" title="Johanna Ey">Johanna "Mother" Ey</a>, born March 4, 1864 in <a href="/wiki/Wickrath" class="mw-redirect" title="Wickrath">Wickrath</a> (today <a href="/wiki/Monchengladbach" class="mw-redirect" title="Monchengladbach">Monchengladbach</a>); † August 27, 1947 in Düsseldorf, gallery owner</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peter_Behrens" title="Peter Behrens">Peter Behrens</a>, born April 14, 1868 in Hamburg-Borgfelde, † February 27, 1940 in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, architect and director of the <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Art_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Düsseldorf Art Academy">Düsseldorf Art Academy</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Kreis" title="Wilhelm Kreis">Wilhelm Kreis</a>, born March 17, 1873 in <a href="/wiki/Eltville" title="Eltville">Eltville</a>, † August 13, 1955 in <a href="/wiki/Bad_Honnef" title="Bad Honnef">Bad Honnef</a>, architect and director of the School of Applied Arts Düsseldorf</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peter_K%C3%BCrten" title="Peter Kürten">Peter Kürten</a>, born May 26, 1883 in <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BClheim_(Cologne)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mülheim (Cologne)">Mülheim am Rhein</a>, † July 2, 1931 in Cologne, called "The Vampire of Düsseldorf", committed in Düsseldorf during the period between February and November 1929 series of sexual homicide</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adolf_Uzarski" title="Adolf Uzarski">Adolf Uzarski</a>, born April 14, 1885 in <a href="/wiki/Ruhrort" title="Ruhrort">Ruhrort</a> (today <a href="/wiki/Duisburg" title="Duisburg">Duisburg</a>), † 14 July 1970 in Düsseldorf, writer, painter and graphic artist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Emil_Fahrenkamp" title="Emil Fahrenkamp">Emil Fahrenkamp</a>, born November 8, 1885 in <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a>, † 24 May 1966 in Ratingen-<a href="/w/index.php?title=Breitscheid_(Ratingen)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Breitscheid (Ratingen) (page does not exist)">Breitscheid</a>, architect and director of <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Art_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Düsseldorf Art Academy">Düsseldorf Art Academy</a> 1937–1945</li>
</ul>
